The kernel launches with `__launch_bounds__(256, 1)` - max 1 wave per SIMD due to high VGPR usage\n2. The issue is that it does all `ds_read` loads first (lines 185-195), then all `v_fmac` MACs (lines 199-223)\n3. Instead of loading ALL input_reg values first then computing, we could load a subset and immediately compute.\n\nLet me think about the loop structure:\n- Outer loop: `for (int oi = KW_PACK*threadIdx.x; oi < num_outputs; oi += KW_PACK*blockDim.x)` - processes BLOCK_H * BLOCK_W output pixels, 2 at a time\n- Each iteration loads KD*KH*KWR = 3*5*3 = 45 input values (each being uint32 containing 2 BF16)\n- Then does 45*2 = 90 MACs per pixel pair\n\nThe problem is that all 90 input_reg values are loaded and kept in registers before any MACs are done. If we interleave - load a smaller chunk then immediately do MACs on that chunk - we can reduce register pressure.\n\n\nI should reduce `input_reg` to hold just a few rows at a time rather than the full KD*KH*KWR*KW_PACK structure.
